## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential/logistic growth to more complex forms with Allee effects, time-varying parameters, or generalized logistic models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced growth at low density)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal carrying capacity)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional-order population dynamics)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-decaying growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * t) (resource depletion over time)
- Hassell-type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P)**c2 (generalized contest/scramble competition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → multiplicative factor (1 - P/K) or rational form 1/(1 + c*P) reducing growth at high density
- Allee effects (cooperative behavior at low density) → additional multiplicative factor (P - threshold) creating a minimum viable population
- Gompertz-type asymmetry → logarithmic terms log(K/P) instead of linear (1 - P/K), giving slower approach to carrying capacity
- Seasonal or periodic environmental forcing → multiplicative sinusoidal modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) on growth parameters
- Metabolic scaling in populations → fractional power P**c with c ≠ 1, reflecting allometric relationships
- Resource depletion over time → time-dependent exponential decay exp(-c*t) multiplying growth terms
- Competition intensity scaling → higher-order polynomial terms in P (P², P³) indicating nonlinear competitive interactions
- Predator-free population with immigration → additive constant term c0 + f(P) representing external population influx

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P**0.333333333333333
```

Let me simplify this. Let me denote `a = 0.7213553457664288`, `b = 6.6511`, `d = 13.538`.

**First term:** `a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P`
= `a*(P/b - 1)*(1 - P/d)*P`
= `a*P*(P/b - 1)(1 - P/d)`
= `a*P*[P/b - P²/(bd) - 1 + P/d]`
= `a*[-P²/(bd) + P²/b + P²/d - P]`
Wait, let me redo:
`(P/b - 1)(1 - P/d) = P/b - P²/(bd) - 1 + P/d`

So first term = `a*P*[P/b - P²/(bd) - 1 + P/d]` = `a*[-P³/(bd) + P²/b + P²/d - P]`

**Second term:** `a*(1 - P/d)*P = a*P - a*P²/d`

**Third term:** `a*P^(1/3)`

Combining first + second terms:
- P³ coefficient: `-a/(bd)`
- P² coefficient: `a/b + a/d - a/d = a/b`
- P coefficient: `-a + a = 0`
- Plus `a*P^(1/3)`

So GT simplifies to:
```
-a/(bd) * P³ + a/b * P² + a*P^(1/3)
```

Let me verify: `-a/(bd)` with b=6.6511, d=13.538:
- `bd = 90.04` approximately
- `-0.7214/90.04 ≈ -0.008012`
- `a/b = 0.7214/6.6511 ≈ 0.10846`

So **GT = c_A * P³ + c_B * P² + c_C * P^(1/3)** where c_A ≈ -0.008, c_B ≈ 0.1085, c_C ≈ 0.7214.

The key basis functions are: **P³, P², and P^(1/3)**.

The critical feature is the **P^(1/3)** term. Any candidate that cannot produce a `P^(1/3)` term cannot match.
